Girls & Boys Hostel Boys PG Google wala mamla thik hua Call kyu kiye the Hi Patner room leke rahega Mtlb hm tum sath Ha Phone kisliye kiye the I am a first year student at IIT DHANBAD pursuing undergraduate degree. I am very interested in the domain of software and data structures and this course will help me to understand it well and will also boost my CV that will help me  get a job after i pass from my institute.  However our annual income is pretty low wrt to the average nation’s income. I’ve no job of my own to carry the expenses to pay for the certificate of this course. In this circumstance, it is very much difficult for me to gather such amount of money for the certificate. Financial Aid will help me take this course without any adverse impact on my monthly essential needs. So I’m badly in need of this financial aid. Receiving this Financial Aid will open for me a new horizon of the world of Coursera courses, which in turn will help me in future. I also plan to complete all assignments on or before time. Programming is an area of interest for me .I have been trying to learn the basics of programming on my own for a year now, but without proper guidance, I am finding it difficult to proceed on my own. A course certificate would not only bolster my self-confidence but help me later in finding a job. Taking this course will help me boost my CV and increase chances of getting job in this domain . I want to gain skills that I feel will be beneficial not only for me and my family but also for organizations and teams with whom I would be working in near future. Oh sorry this is Inheritance explanation 🤦 Yeah Usually, interfaces are used to provide INDEPENDENT functionality. Like the ```Iterator``` interface allows objects to be iterated over, and the ```Runnable``` interface allows processes to run in a separate thread. Definitely look to libraries for inspiration, and feel free to copy whatever you like. Smart! Agreed But I feel that the only time you should be using libraries is for prototypes, never for the final version of an app/website. This way, you aren't really using the library, but you also are ...... Ohh ESPECIALLY CSS/JavaScript libraries. Oh .. So I should not use Bootstrap, Materialize CSS, Tailwind CSS, etc for my projects... Unless the library ADDS critical functionality (eg: PDF parser, WebSocket management) you should think twice before using it. Oh Again, the decision is up to you, but I don't like to use these libraries. You can achieve the same outcome with 0.1% of the code. And I am not even joking, try measuring code coverage in DevTools. What is a CDN is used? If* We're having real talks at 2.35 AM 👏👏 A CDN can only speed up the download times. What I meant that most (small) projects do not even use 2-5% of the code in a huge library like jQuery or BootStrap. Agreed, but it only imports the code that is called... So even if you are using a CDN, and the library is 10,000 lines, then you are only using 100-150 lines. Which seems like a MASSIVE waste. But it looks like a customisable yet limited platform specifically created for development of apps for internal business use something like a project management app. It's an interesting move of Amazon's part. They are trying to migrate people who are using Google docs or microsoft excel to this platform which is powered by AWS. How exactly/ This is an app development platform, right? Not an Excel or Google Sheets clone. Businesses use spreadsheets for managing projects that is what they are trying to replace. Not something like data analysis or financial analysis done using spreadsheets They are basically trying to solve the problem of using spreadsheets where they are not supposed to be conventionally used . Ab khatam😂 Idt java me there is something like flushall() Scanner operates on a token stream, as opposed to BufferedReader, which operates on lines. So, imagine Scanner gets the inputs: Didn't see the code Yes ik Okay Now, it is important to understand what the ```nextInt()``` method actually does. Explain sir ```nextInt()``` will try to find an *Integer token*, while ignoring any whitespace. An Integer token is defined as ```/(+|-)?\d+/``` Meaning + or -, followed by one or more digits. Okay So Scanner reads the token stream, finds 10 and returns it. Now the stream is: ```\nHello, World!\n``` Again, we must understand what the ```nextLine()``` method does. ```nextLine()``` is actually a special method, that breaks the boundries of a tokenizer. It simply starts reading from the current point, and returns *all characters* till it finds a newline (```\n```). (without the newline) So calling ```nextLine()``` on ```\nHello, World!\n``` will start reading, the stop at the first character because it is a newline. So basically Which means it will return an empty string. Yes. Alright. No problem. Ohhhhh Okayyy Ik this Too much damn C me this had a function idk java me kyu nahi dala... Flushall na?
